I had my car towed about 15 miles at rush hour, but he was still kind enough to knock some money off his originally quoted price. He doesn't act like this job is a chore, as this is his own business. He is efficient, kind and was generous enough to let me ride with him to my destination (mechanic). He took are of my car and me. I felt very lucky to find him and would highly recommend calling!<//review>

<text>After recently purchasing a house, we needed to have some minor electrical corrected, and several fans/control switches/can lights/dimmer switches and a stand-alone RV power outlet installed. We heard about Raceway through our realtor (who had used them for a number of years for their own properties). On the day of installation, Billy and Sam arrived on time, and were very professional and personable. Billy took our requests/needs into account for the install, and suggested very logical options that would work for the room size. We went with Billy's recommendations, and everything turned out excellent! They both worked very efficiently and answered any questions we had along the way.
Thank you guys!

A few weeks after the install, we noticed one of the fans (Brand: Minka Aire)  was making a ticking noise while operating at higher speeds. Raceway sent Sam to take a look. He figured out the problem in a few minutes, and made the correction (putting two 2" sections of gasket material 180deg apart between the ceiling and the base cover). No more ticking!!
Per the fan retailer and Raceway, this is a common issue with this brand of fans.

We intend to use Raceway for future projects.
Highly recommended!< /text>< pictures>
None</pictures>

<rate>5</rate>< Review>
I stopped by to search for what I learned to be the smallest size DXL sells, but I still enjoyed looking around the store for ideas for a tall friend of mine who has issues finding clothes. The customer service here is excellent! They're readily available to help you find what you need and answer any questions you might have. They even offer to order an item you need shipped online while you're in the store seeing items in person.
While their prices are more expensive than what you'd pay at another store, they do have a small discounted section in the back of the store near the tailoring mirrors. I recommend this store and company to those looking for quality long and tall clothes.< /Review>

<review>Manhattan's in the desert is a restaurant that specializes in Delicatessen Foods. They have a large menu and the portions tend to be on the generous side. The food there is usually pretty good and the service was very attentive. If you're looking 4 a scrumptious sandwich this would be the place to get it. The restaurant also has a bakery that tends to sell items that are on the very large size. If you're going for lunch or dinner make sure you ask the waiter to bring you out pickles. They have pickled tomatoes dill pickles and kosher style pickles. They also make delicious omelettes add egg dishes and french toast dishes. They have a lox and bagel plate that is quite good. Manhattan's in the desert is a good place for breakfast lunch or dinner.< /review>< pictures>

<userid>103539864198558349549< /userid><Name>Ken Privett<//Name>< date>
1564285236279</date>
<Rating>4</Rating>< text>
Although this is a long time, well established restaurant here, tonight was the first time I went after all these years visiting and living here.
The service was outstanding and very personable - I loved my waitress. The food was good with large portions. Plenty of parking. On a Saturday night, at 6:30 pm, in the middle of 113¬∞ heat, the place wasn't completely full but almost.
I had clipped a $11.99 summer dinner coupon that motivated me to come by. However, it was part of their normal menu, but no big deal. I'm sure they will continue for the remainder of the summer season.
Large and varied menu that should handle most people.
I ordered the turkey dinner which came with soup or salad, roast turkey slices, and two vegetable sides for $11.99. Drink was extra. As I said earlier, the portions were very generous and I left stuffed. However, I couldn't resist getting a Key Lime Bar to go. With tax and tip, the total was under thirty.
A couple of weeks ago I went to Sherman's, which is surprisingly similar in every way. However, of the two, the food and service at Manhattan was much better. Cost was the same for their dinner special.
With Manhattan's other restaurant in Palm Desert closing recently, for which I hadn't heard anything good about, I was hesitant to come here. But not now as I look forward to coming back soon.
Definitely a place I would recommend.</text>

<Name>Ryan Freeman< /Name>< time>
1524594666590< /time>
<rate>4< /rate>< text>
Great New York style eatery.  Lots of options.  Perhaps too many...
Food-wise:  You can never go wrong with a salad or sandwich, which are all HUGE.  Dinners are very traditional.  No frills or surprises.  What lacks in quality is made up for in quantity.  And don't be afraid to customize or specify preferences.  They are awesome with getting you exactly what you want.
Desserts often look better than they taste, unfortunately.  Most are quite dense and all are served cold.  Carrot Cake is always a win though and a cinnamon roll ONLY IF you eat it there, but be sure to order it warmed with extra icing.  Otherwise they are typically pretty dry.
Last, whether you dine-in or take-out, don't forget to ask for pickles, which are hommade and served with homemade pickled green tomatoes and sauerkraut.
Expect dinner to run $30 a head inclusive of t&t.<//text>

<date>1478482715178< /date><rate>5< /rate><Review>It's on the must visit list when in Palm Springs. You know as soon as you walk in there's something good going on here. Also, that you better be careful ordering. The pastries are excellent, and huge. Most of the food orders are as well.

<text>Interesting and tasty spins on a lot of standard favorites, like Huevos Rancheros. Same twists go for their French Toast Monte Christo; so good! The menu has a broad selectiin. Be forewarned, portions are large. All the better to take a doggie bag for an later snack.

<Rating>2</Rating>< review>
Just got back from Palm Springs. This used to be my favorite restaurant. Service was great. Asked if we wanted drinks within 2 minutes of sitting down and the drinks were on the table in under 5 minutes. My wife had the steak sandwich which she said was excellent. 8 ounce Ribeye on a roll with fries. it looked good too.
I had the super combo Pastrami, Turkey and Corned Beef on Rye. All you could taste was the turkey but the worst part was the bread tasted like it had been thawed out in the Microwave. the center of the bread was ice cold and the rest was hard and dry like what happens when you microwave something 10 seconds too long. I have read that this place was starting to go cheap to keep the prices down but when you truly skip on quality and get caught..................I'll go elsewhere. I would say even though my wife loved her sandwich, mine was the worst sandwich I ever have had. I'll drive by next time.< /review>

< review>
This review if for the Highway 111 location -  not the Palm Canyon (unfortunately, they don't appear to have their Google+ page set up for the Highway 111 venue as of yet).

Discovered this place by accident while driving down Hwy 111. Being a native New York, I of course noticed the word "Manhattan" right away and was intrigued by the prospects of "Manhattan in the Desert".  Stopped in with family for lunch and was not disappointed!  The decor is upscale casual with very comfortable booths.  Large black and white vintage prints of NY scenes hang on the walls.  The menu is huge! Took 10 minutes just to make a decision!  Decided to go with a classic Ham, Salami and Swiss sandwich on rye with side of potato salad.  The sandwich size matched the menu - again, huge!  Delicious.  Also, they have a bakery with assorted rugala and my favorite, huge black and white cookies!  Terrific place with friendly staff as was the manager, Itai was very friendly and grateful for our business.  Will be sure to visit again next time I'm in the desert!</review>

< Text>
This is the second time we have eaten lunch in Manhattan in the Desert and the second time we were disappointed. This time around it appears the restaurant has been updated with new upholstery and some artwork but the quality if the food and taste remains unchanged, disappointing. The service was at best fair, no attention to customer needs or satisfaction and inattentive. Had to wave down a bussboy twice to get the waiters attention. The pastrami sandwich was way too fatty, I like the meat juicy and of course expect a little fat to keep it moist and most of all tasty, but this second visit produced the same disappointing lunch, tastless pastrami. There are two N.Y. type delis in the desert, as of now there is only one TRUE, New York deli (take it from this long time New Yorker who's eaten the real deal for thirty plus years) and that's Sherman's. I like the one located in Palm Desert better than the one in Palm Springs. We'll never give Manhattan another chance.</Text>
